## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship in materials, where stress typically increases with strain through elastic and hardening mechanisms, while decreasing with temperature due to thermal softening. Classical constitutive models often separate these effects into multiplicative or additive components.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic behavior at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus: sigma = c0 * (c1 - T) * epsilon (linear elasticity with linearly decreasing modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Hollomon-type strain hardening)
- Power-law with thermal softening (linear): sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 - c3 * T) (hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook type: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 - c4 * T**c5) (combined hardening and thermal softening)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (power-law hardening with Arrhenius-type thermal effect)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 * (c1 - exp(c2 * epsilon)) (saturating stress-strain curve)
- Voce with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * (c1 - exp(c2 * epsilon)) * exp(c3 * T) (saturating hardening with thermal softening)
- Ludwik model: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Ludwik with temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(c3 * T) (Ludwik with exponential thermal softening)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 + epsilon)**(c2) * (c3 - c4 * T) (nonlinear elastic-plastic with thermal effect)
- Hyperbolic tangent hardening: sigma = c0 * tanh(c1 * epsilon) * (c2 - c3 * T) (saturating hardening with linear softening)
- Polynomial thermal modulus: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 + c2 * T + c3 * T**2) (quadratic temperature dependence of modulus)
- Swift model with temperature: sigma = c0 * (c1 + epsilon)**c2 * exp(c3 * T) (Swift hardening with exponential thermal softening)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Multiplicative decomposition of strain hardening and thermal softening → sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T), where f is increasing and g is decreasing
- Strain hardening saturation at large strains → Use (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or tanh(c*epsilon) rather than unbounded power laws
- Thermal softening toward a melting point → Factor (c0 - T)**c1 or (1 - c0*T**c1) representing zero stress at melting temperature
- Yield stress offset → Additive constant c0 in stress representing initial yield before hardening: sigma = c0 + f(epsilon)
- Arrhenius-type thermal activation → exp(c0 * T) or exp(c0 / T) capturing thermally activated dislocation mechanisms
- Concave-up vs concave-down stress-strain → Power exponent c < 1 gives concave-down (hardening saturation), c > 1 gives concave-up (accelerating hardening)
- Temperature-dependent hardening rate → Coupling where hardening exponent or coefficient itself depends on T: epsilon**g(T)
- Elastic-to-plastic transition smoothing → Smooth transition functions like (epsilon**c0)/(c1 + epsilon**c0) to model yield without discontinuity
